## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt with inputs t and concentration A indicates an ordinary differential equation governing how a chemical species concentration changes over time. Common kinetics models express dA_dt as a function of A (reaction order, saturation/inhibition, reversibility) and sometimes explicitly of t (time-varying feed, deactivation, or changing conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption; e.g., surface-limited or excess reactant regime)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like decay, well-mixed first-order reaction)
- Second-order decay (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with identical reactant A)
- General nth-order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical order; fits non-integer kinetics)
- Autocatalytic growth with quadratic term: dA_dt = c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (self-amplification with depletion/termination; logistic-like kinetics in chemistry)
- Reversible first-order to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (net relaxation toward A_eq = c1 / c0)
- Reversible with equilibrium concentration parameter: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (linear return to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Saturating (Monod-type) consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate saturates at high A due to capacity/active-site limitation)
- Substrate inhibition / self-inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1 + c2 * A**2) (rate decreases at high A due to inhibition or crowding)
- Autocatalysis with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) - c2 * A (chain-branching with limiting step and termination)
- Time-dependent forcing/feed (exponential): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(-c2 * t) (decaying input/source or transient catalyst effect)
- Catalyst/activity deactivation multiplying kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate constant decreases over time)
- Periodic driving/photochemical modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (time-modulated source/sink, e.g., pulsed irradiation)
- Stretched-exponential effective kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t**c2) (distributed time scales / complex media effects)
- Mixed-order (sum of channels): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order loss pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order identification: if dA_dt scales linearly with A, use -c*A; if curvature increases strongly with A, consider -c*A**2 or -c*A**n.
- Equilibrium relaxation: sign change around a nonzero A indicates a restoring form like -c*(A-c_eq) or -c*A + c_source.
- Parallel pathways: sums of terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) represent multiple simultaneous mechanisms with different molecularities.
- Saturation due to limited active sites/capacity: rational forms like -c0*A/(A+c1) produce a rate that approaches a constant magnitude at high A.
- Inhibition at high concentration: adding higher-power terms in the denominator (A + c1 + c2*A**2) creates a peak rate at intermediate A and slowing at large A.
- Autocatalysis/chain branching: positive feedback terms (e.g., +c*A or +c*A**2) combined with loss terms can yield rapid acceleration followed by stabilization/decline.
- Time-varying conditions (feed, light, mixing changes): explicit t terms (sin, exp, polynomial in t) indicate non-autonomous kinetics rather than pure state dependence.
- Deactivation/aging: multiplicative exp(-c*t) on A-dependent rates models a time-decreasing effective rate constant (catalyst poisoning, radical scavenger buildup).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK5)
============================================================
GT: -c0*sqrt(A) + c1*_f*A**c2
Candidate formulas: 54

GT is the fixed function (independent of \(t\)):
\[
0.5229500625821207\,A^{1/3}\;-\;0.3254156367450257\,\sqrt{A}.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) have no remaining \(t\)-dependence after parameter choice, and (ii) reduce exactly to a linear combination of \(A^{1/3}\) and \(\sqrt{A}\) with those coefficients (for all \(A\) in the domain). Also note candidates often use \(\sqrt{|A|}\) or \(|A|^{1/3}\); these cannot equal \(\sqrt{A}\) or \(A^{1/3}\) for all real \(A\). A match is still possible if we can set parameters so the expression uses \(A^{1/3}\) and \(\sqrt{A}\) exactly (not absolute values), or if the candidate already uses \(\sqrt{A}\) and \(A^{1/3}\).

---

### 1. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Set \(c2=0\) to remove sine. But \(|A|^{1/3}\neq A^{1/3}\) for all real \(A\). If we set \(c1=0\), we lose the \(A^{1/3}\) term. So cannot match GT. **No**.

### 2. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Then we have \(A^{1/3}\) (good) but \(\sqrt{|A|}\neq \sqrt{A}\) for all real \(A\). If \(c1=0\), we lose the \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 3. Same as (2) plus \(+c5\)
Need \(c2=0\) and \(c5=0\), still stuck with \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 4. \(A^{c0}c1 + c2|A|^{c3} + c4 e^{Ac5} + c6\)
To match GT (two power terms only), must set \(c4=0, c6=0\). Then need \(A^{c0}\) and \(|A|^{c3}\) to become \(A^{1/3}\) and \(\sqrt{A}\). But \(|A|^{c3}\) cannot equal \(\sqrt{A}\) for all real \(A\). If we avoid absolute by setting \(c2=0\), we lose one needed term. **No**.

### 5. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 + c3 t/(Ac4+c5) + c6/(Ac4+c5)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), must set \(c3=0\). Also must remove rational-in-\(A\) term: set \(c6=0\). Then need \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\) issue. **No**.

### 6. \(A^{c0}c1 + c2|A|^{c3} + c4 t/(c5 t+c6) + c7/(c5 t+c6)\)
To eliminate \(t\)-dependence for all \(t\), must set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\) (otherwise nonconstant in \(t\)). Then reduces to power terms with \(|A|^{c3}\) again. Same obstacle. **No**.

### 7. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + A c1/(c2 t+c3) + c4|A|^{1/3} + c5/(c2 t+c3)\)
To remove \(t\): need \(c1=0\) and \(c5=0\) (or \(c2=0\) making denominator constant, but then you still get an \(A\) term and/or constant term not in GT unless zeroed). With \(c1=c5=0\), still has \(|A|^{1/3}\) not \(A^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 8. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1/(c2 t+c3) + c4\sqrt{|A|} + c5/(c2 t+c3)\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c1=0, c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 9. Same as (8) plus \(+c5\) and \(+c6/(c2 t+c3)\)
Need \(c1=0, c6=0, c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 10. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1/(A c2+c3) + c4\sqrt{|A|} + c5/(A c2+c3)\)
No \(t\), but has rational terms in \(A\). To match GT, must set \(c1=0, c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 11. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + A c1/(A c2+c3) + c4|A|^{1/3} + c5/(A c2+c3)\)
Set \(c1=0, c5=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 12. Like (10) plus constant and extra rational term
Must set rational terms zero: \(c1=0, c6=0\), constant \(c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 13. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\)
Need \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\) mismatch unless \(c1=0\) (then missing \(A^{1/3}\)). **No**.

### 14. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2\)
Need \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\) mismatch unless \(c1=0\) (then missing \(\sqrt{A}\)). **No**.

### 15. \(A^{c0}c1 + c2|A|^{c3}\)
Same absolute-value obstacle for the \(\sqrt{A}\) term. **No**.

### 16. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A c1(c2+t)^{c3} + c4\sqrt{|A|} + c5\)
To remove \(t\), must set \(c1=0\). Then need \(c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 17. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 + c3\log(Ac4+1)\)
Must set \(c3=0\), \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 18. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 e^{c3 t}\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 19. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2 e^{c3 t}\)
Set \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 20. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 t/(c3 t+c4) + c5/(c3 t+c4)\)
To remove \(t\), must set \(c2=0, c5=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 21. Like (20) plus constant
Need \(c3=0\)?? Actually to remove \(t\)-dependence robustly: set \(c3=0\) makes denominators constant but leaves a linear \(t\) term unless \(c3\) there is different; safest: set \(c3=0\) gives \(c3 t/(c4 t+c5)=0\) anyway since numerator uses \(c3\); but there is \(c6/(c4 t+c5)\) still \(t\)-dependent unless \(c6=0\). In any case must kill those terms and constant \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 22. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2 t/(c3 t+c4) + c5/(c3 t+c4)\)
Kill \(t\)-terms: \(c2=0, c5=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 23. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 + c3 t (A+c4)^{c5}\)
Must set \(c3=0\), \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 24. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 e^{A c3} + c4\)
Must set \(c2=0, c4=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 25. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sqrt{|A|}\)
We could set \(c1=1/3\) to make second term another \(A^{1/3}\), but we need a \(\sqrt{A}\) term and \(\sqrt{|A|}\) is wrong for all real \(A\). If set \(c3=0\), lose sqrt term. **No**.

### 26. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3|A|^{1/3}\)
We can set \(c1=1/3\) to get \(A^{1/3}\) from \(A^{c1}c2\), and we already have \(\sqrt(A)\) (good). But there is an extra \(|A|^{1/3}\) term unless \(c3=0\). If \(c3=0\), expression becomes
\[
c0\sqrt(A) + c2 A^{1/3}.
\]
This can match GT exactly by choosing
\[
c2 = 0.5229500625821207,\quad c0 = -0.3254156367450257.
\]
No \(t\)-dependence. **Yes, matches.**

### 27. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\log(c3 t+1)\)
Must set \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 28. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2\log(c3 t+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 29. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2 e^{A c3}\)
Set \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 30. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2 e^{A c3}\)
Set \(c2=0\). Still \(|A|^{1/3}\). **No**.

### 31. \(A^{1/3}c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sqrt{|A|} + c4\)
Need \(c4=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\) issue. **No**.

### 32. \(A^{1/3}c0 + c1\sqrt{|A|} + c2\log(Ac3+1)\)
Set \(c2=0\). Still \(\sqrt{|A|}\). **No**.

### 33. \(\sqrt(A)c0 + c1|A|^{1/3} + c2\log(Ac3+1)\)
